    <h5><b>Official websites use .gov</b></h5>
<p>A .gov website belongs to an official government organization in the United States.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text">
<div data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-aa4550c581&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;nycgov/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-09-27T19:32:19Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h5>&lt;b>Secure .gov websites use HTTPS&lt;/b>&lt;/h5>\r\n&lt;p>A lock (&amp;#x1f512;) or https:// means you’ve safely connected to the .gov website.     <h5><b>Secure .gov websites use HTTPS</b></h5>
<p>A lock (&#x1f512;) or https:// means you’ve safely connected to the .gov website. Share sensitive information only on official, secure websites.</p>

  <script>
   const isSearchPage = document.body.classList.contains("searchpage");
   const isMainSite = document.body.classList.contains("main-site");
   const customSearchBox = document.querySelector('#coveo-search-btn-redirect custom-search-box');
   const mainHost = customSearchBox?.getAttribute("data-search-url");
   if (!isMainSite) {
     const searchBoxes = document.querySelectorAll('custom-search-box[data-search-url]');
     const url = new URL(window.location.href);
     const host = url.host;
     const pathSegments = url.pathname.split('/').filter(Boolean);
     const isoCodeRegex = /^[a-z]{2}(-[A-Z]{2})?$/;
     const isSameHost = mainHost.includes(host);
     const searchPageHost = new URL(mainHost).host;
     const isSameDomain = (host === searchPageHost);
     let site = host;
     if (isSameHost) {
       const relevantSegment = isoCodeRegex.test(pathSegments[0]) ? pathSegments[1] : pathSegments[0] || '';
       site = host + "/" + relevantSegment;
     }
     customSearchBox.setAttribute('is-external-domain', !isSameDomain);
     searchBoxes.forEach(box => {
       const currentUrl = box.getAttribute('data-search-url');
       const newUrl = currentUrl + "?sitesearch=" + site;
       box.setAttribute('data-search-url', newUrl);
     });
   }
   if (isSearchPage) {
     const redirectEl = document.getElementById("coveo-search-btn-redirect");
     if (redirectEl) { redirectEl.remove(); }
   } else {
     const resultsEl = document.getElementById("coveo-search-btn-results");
     if (resultsEl) { resultsEl.remove(); }
   }
  </script>

          <h1 class="nyc-hero__title" data-heading-only="false" data-has-bread="true">
            Ahead of Opening Day, Mamdani Administration Breaks Ground on Project to Improve Bronx Crosstown Bus Service and Safety Near Yankee Stadium
          </h1>
          <div>
            <div class="nyc-hero__description text">
              <p>March 24, 2026</p>
            </div>
            
          </div>
        </div>
        
      </div>
    </div>

<div class="text">
<div data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-99f8280a76&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;nycgov/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2026-03-24T15:53:37Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p style=\&#34;text-align: center;\&#34;>&lt;i>Bx6 Select Bus Service at East 161st Street and Sherman Avenue&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>NEW YORK &lt;/b>– New York City Mayor Zohran Kwame Mamdani, New York City Department of Transportation (NYC DOT) Commissioner Mike Flynn and Department of Design and Construction (DDC) Acting Commissioner Eduardo del Valle today announced the start of a major project to improve Bronx crosstown bus service and street safety near Yankee Stadium.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The project will add westbound bus-only lanes, including converting the 161st Street underpass to buses only. The redesign also includes pedestrian safety upgrades and new amenities for bus riders — such as bus shelters, benches and leaning bars, along with pedestrian refuges and infrastructure to make boarding buses safer and more accessible.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>With baseball’s Opening Day later this week, the project will speed up bus service and improve safety around Yankee Stadium, which sees more than three million visitors each year. The corridor serves 25,000 daily riders on the Bx6 Select Bus Service (SBS) line.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“Unfortunately, as the Mayor of New York City, I must deliver fast and reliable buses for Yankees fans as well,” said &lt;b>Mayor Mamdani&lt;/b>. “I can think of no better way to welcome the start of baseball season than by breaking ground on a project that will make commutes faster, streets safer and daily life a little easier for tens of thousands of New Yorkers every day.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“Improving the bus-rider and pedestrian experiences for those who visit or live in the South Bronx is a home run for all New Yorkers,” said &lt;b>NYC DOT Commissioner Mike Flynn&lt;/b>. “From Fordham Road to Yankee Stadium, this administration is doubling down to deliver better buses and safer streets.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“This project will help link some of the busiest areas of Manhattan and the Bronx with a fast and safe bus route and access to vital civic resources, moving closer to the administration’s goal of a great bus network for every neighborhood,” said &lt;b>NYC DDC Acting Commissioner Eduardo del Valle&lt;/b>. “DDC is phasing the construction so as to not interfere with baseball season but we are hard at work in other areas so that we can meet the 2028 completion date.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“We are pleased that the City is moving forward with the long-planned effort to make 161st Street more bus friendly,” said &lt;b>MTA New York City Transit Executive Vice President of Buses Frank Farrell&lt;/b>. “It’s good news for South Bronx bus riders, and we look forward to celebrating even more improvements throughout the five boroughs because nothing makes buses faster than clear streets.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The project will reconstruct and redesign East 161st Street from Ruppert Place to Morris Avenue, including portions of East 163rd Street between Washington Avenue and Tiffany Street, as well as segments of the Bx6-SBS route in Manhattan.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>As part of the redesign, the City will create a fully protected, center-running bus lane along East 161st Street from Concourse Village West to just west of River Avenue — one of the only corridors of its kind in New York City. Construction has already begun on East 163rd Street between Intervale Avenue and Tiffany Street.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}" id="text-99f8280a76" class="cmp-text ">
    <p style="	text-align: center;
"><i>Bx6 Select Bus Service at East 161st Street and Sherman Avenue </i></p>
<p> </p>
<p><b>NEW YORK </b>– New York City Mayor Zohran Kwame Mamdani, New York City Department of Transportation (NYC DOT) Commissioner Mike Flynn and Department of Design and Construction (DDC) Acting Commissioner Eduardo del Valle today announced the start of a major project to improve Bronx crosstown bus service and street safety near Yankee Stadium.</p>
<p>The project will add westbound bus-only lanes, including converting the 161st Street underpass to buses only. The redesign also includes pedestrian safety upgrades and new amenities for bus riders — such as bus shelters, benches and leaning bars, along with pedestrian refuges and infrastructure to make boarding buses safer and more accessible.</p>
<p>With baseball’s Opening Day later this week, the project will speed up bus service and improve safety around Yankee Stadium, which sees more than three million visitors each year. The corridor serves 25,000 daily riders on the Bx6 Select Bus Service (SBS) line.</p>
<p>“Unfortunately, as the Mayor of New York City, I must deliver fast and reliable buses for Yankees fans as well,” said <b>Mayor Mamdani</b>. “I can think of no better way to welcome the start of baseball season than by breaking ground on a project that will make commutes faster, streets safer and daily life a little easier for tens of thousands of New Yorkers every day.”</p>
<p>“Improving the bus-rider and pedestrian experiences for those who visit or live in the South Bronx is a home run for all New Yorkers,” said <b>NYC DOT Commissioner Mike Flynn</b>. “From Fordham Road to Yankee Stadium, this administration is doubling down to deliver better buses and safer streets.”</p>
<p>“This project will help link some of the busiest areas of Manhattan and the Bronx with a fast and safe bus route and access to vital civic resources, moving closer to the administration’s goal of a great bus network for every neighborhood,” said <b>NYC DDC Acting Commissioner Eduardo del Valle</b>. “DDC is phasing the construction so as to not interfere with baseball season but we are hard at work in other areas so that we can meet the 2028 completion date.”</p>
<p>“We are pleased that the City is moving forward with the long-planned effort to make 161st Street more bus friendly,” said <b>MTA New York City Transit Executive Vice President of Buses Frank Farrell</b>. “It’s good news for South Bronx bus riders, and we look forward to celebrating even more improvements throughout the five boroughs because nothing makes buses faster than clear streets.”</p>
<p>The project will reconstruct and redesign East 161st Street from Ruppert Place to Morris Avenue, including portions of East 163rd Street between Washington Avenue and Tiffany Street, as well as segments of the Bx6-SBS route in Manhattan.</p>
<p>As part of the redesign, the City will create a fully protected, center-running bus lane along East 161st Street from Concourse Village West to just west of River Avenue — one of the only corridors of its kind in New York City. Construction has already begun on East 163rd Street between Intervale Avenue and Tiffany Street.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image">
<figure data-cmp-is="image" data-cmp-src="/mayors-office/news/2026/03/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr/_jcr_content/root/container_481968979/container/initialContent/image_1183077443.coreimg{.width}.png/1774367577114/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr--2.png" data-asset-id="f698c087-5bf8-495e-9793-5eaafbbc4cd8" data-cmp-filereference="/content/dam/nycgov/mayors-office/images/press-releases/2026/03/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr--2.png" id="image-f0570d6c51" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-f0570d6c51&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;core/wcm/components/image/v3/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2026-03-24T15:52:57Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;f698c087-5bf8-495e-9793-5eaafbbc4cd8&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2026-03-24T15:50:10Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/nycgov/mayors-office/images/press-releases/2026/03/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr--2.png&#34;,&#34;xdm:tags&#34;:[&#34;properties:orientation/landscape&#34;],&#34;xdm:smartTags&#34;:{&#34;event photography&#34;:0.779}}}}" data-cmp-hook-image="imageV3" class="cmp-image " data-caption="false" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject">
  
    <img src="/mayors-office/news/2026/03/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr/_jcr_content/root/container_481968979/container/initialContent/image_1183077443.coreimg.png/1774367577114/ahead-of-opening-day--mamdani-administration-breaks-ground-on-pr--2.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" width="624" height="380" alt="A map shows Bx6 SBS route, dated September 3, 2017"/>
  
  
  
  <div class="cmp-image__credits">
    <button type="button" aria-label="Image credits" aria-expanded="false">
      <i class="i-ph:x"></i>
      <img src="/etc.clientlibs/nycgov/clientlibs/clientlib-site/resources/images/photo-icon.svg" alt=""/>
    </button>
    <div class="cmp-image__credits--credit-text" aria-hidden="true">
      <p>Photo by NYC</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  
  
</figure>

    

</div>
<div class="text">
<div data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-451fb49451&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;nycgov/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2026-03-24T15:53:54Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p style=\&#34;text-align: center;\&#34;>&lt;i>Bx6 Select Bus Service at East 161st Street and Sherman Avenue&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p style=\&#34;text-align: center;\&#34;>&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;u>Better Bus Service&lt;/u>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The project will upgrade the existing eastbound bus tunnel under the Grand Concourse to bus-only use in both directions. Currently, the tunnel is restricted to eastbound buses. To complement this change, three blocks of westbound 161st Street on either side of the tunnel will also be converted to bus-only, easing congestion at key bottlenecks.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The City will install full-length concrete boarding islands along center-running bus lanes to improve safety, shorten pedestrian crossing distances and prevent vehicles from blocking bus lanes. Additional improvements include sidewalk extensions, known as bus bulbs, at bus stops along the Bx6 route to speed up boarding and create space for seating and bus shelters.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;u>Improved Pedestrian Safety&lt;/u>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Curb extensions, medians and pedestrian refuge islands will shorten crossing distances and improve visibility. Existing painted safety features will be upgraded to concrete and extend the sidewalk out to new curblines.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Pedestrian refuge islands have been shown to reduce deaths and serious injuries by 35.5%, while curb and sidewalk extensions reduce them by 34.1%. The City will also rebuild, expand and landscape medians at East 161st Street and River Avenue, just outside of Yankee Stadium.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;u>Infrastructure Improvements&lt;/u>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The project includes 370 ADA-compliant pedestrian ramps, 57 new trees and approximately 8,000 plantings of grass and perennials. More than 100 new street lighting and traffic signal poles will be installed, and 16 fire hydrants will be upgraded.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Crews will reconstruct about 45,000 square yards of roadway and upgrade or add more than 180,000 square feet of sidewalk. Below ground, more than 4,500 feet of water mains and sewers will be upgraded, and additional catch basins will be added to improve drainage.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The project follows extensive community engagement and has support from local community boards. Construction is expected to continue through 2028.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>City agencies have developed a traffic mitigation plan to minimize traffic disruptions during Yankees games.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“Public transit is not a side issue in working-class communities—it is the infrastructure of daily life,” said &lt;b>New York&lt;/b> &lt;b>State Senator Robert Jackson&lt;/b>. “For the thousands who rely on the Bx6 each day, a slow bus is not an inconvenience—it is time taken from work, from school and from family. For too long, communities like the Bronx have carried that burden through delayed service and unsafe streets. This project begins to change that—delivering faster buses, safer corridors and a system that respects the urgency of people’s lives. Because when transit works, opportunity is no longer out of reach—it arrives on time.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“I’m grateful to Mayor Mamdani, NYC DOT, and DDC for advancing these important improvements along the Bx6 corridor in Manhattan, strengthening a critical connection between Manhattan and the Bronx,” said &lt;b>Manhattan Borough President Brad Hoylman-Sigal&lt;/b>. “With Opening Day here, it’s especially important that we’re investing in faster, more reliable bus service and safer streets for the thousands of New Yorkers traveling between our boroughs each day. I look forward to the benefits for riders and neighborhoods on both sides of the Harlem River.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“Get ready for a strike down the middle! Better bus service and safer streets go hand in hand, and this project delivers both,” said &lt;b>New York City Council Majority Leader Shaun Abreu&lt;/b>. “This is an important step from the City to deliver on its promise of fast, reliable buses. I&#39;m excited to see this investment in protected, center-running bus lanes and look forward to working with the Mayor to bring more projects like this to neighborhoods across the city.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“Fully protected center-running bus lanes, plus other upgrades for speed, safety and comfort, are good news for Bronx riders and show the type of commitment riders want to see citywide,” said &lt;b>Betsy Plum, Executive Director, Riders Alliance&lt;/b>. “We look forward to the rollout this spring and are eager to see these bus service improvements show up in our lives and take root in our community. Projects like these that save time and dignify bus commutes are an essential part of building a city that all New Yorkers can afford.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>“The Bx6 is a critical crosstown corridor whose buses have been moving too slowly for far too long,” said &lt;b>Ben Furnas, Executive Director, Transportation Alternatives&lt;/b>. “We&#39;re thrilled this project will include a fully-protected two-way center-running bus lane — a gold-standard design which will speed up travel for tens of thousands of New Yorkers, including those trying to catch the game at Yankee Stadium! Paired with new safety infrastructure for pedestrians and cyclists, this ambitious project will bring much-needed upgrades to the streets of the Bronx.”&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p style=\&#34;text-align: center;\&#34;>###&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}" id="text-451fb49451" class="cmp-text ">
    <p style="	text-align: center;
"><i>Bx6 Select Bus Service at East 161st Street and Sherman Avenue </i></p>
<p style="	text-align: center;
"> </p>
<p><u>Better Bus Service</u></p>
<p>The project will upgrade the existing eastbound bus tunnel under the Grand Concourse to bus-only use in both directions. Currently, the tunnel is restricted to eastbound buses. To complement this change, three blocks of westbound 161st Street on either side of the tunnel will also be converted to bus-only, easing congestion at key bottlenecks.</p>
<p>The City will install full-length concrete boarding islands along center-running bus lanes to improve safety, shorten pedestrian crossing distances and prevent vehicles from blocking bus lanes. Additional improvements include sidewalk extensions, known as bus bulbs, at bus stops along the Bx6 route to speed up boarding and create space for seating and bus shelters.</p>
<p><u>Improved Pedestrian Safety</u></p>
<p>Curb extensions, medians and pedestrian refuge islands will shorten crossing distances and improve visibility. Existing painted safety features will be upgraded to concrete and extend the sidewalk out to new curblines.</p>
<p>Pedestrian refuge islands have been shown to reduce deaths and serious injuries by 35.5%, while curb and sidewalk extensions reduce them by 34.1%. The City will also rebuild, expand and landscape medians at East 161st Street and River Avenue, just outside of Yankee Stadium.</p>
<p><u>Infrastructure Improvements</u></p>
<p>The project includes 370 ADA-compliant pedestrian ramps, 57 new trees and approximately 8,000 plantings of grass and perennials. More than 100 new street lighting and traffic signal poles will be installed, and 16 fire hydrants will be upgraded.</p>
<p>Crews will reconstruct about 45,000 square yards of roadway and upgrade or add more than 180,000 square feet of sidewalk. Below ground, more than 4,500 feet of water mains and sewers will be upgraded, and additional catch basins will be added to improve drainage.</p>
<p>The project follows extensive community engagement and has support from local community boards. Construction is expected to continue through 2028.</p>
<p>City agencies have developed a traffic mitigation plan to minimize traffic disruptions during Yankees games.</p>
<p>“Public transit is not a side issue in working-class communities—it is the infrastructure of daily life,” said <b>New York</b> <b>State Senator Robert Jackson</b>. “For the thousands who rely on the Bx6 each day, a slow bus is not an inconvenience—it is time taken from work, from school and from family. For too long, communities like the Bronx have carried that burden through delayed service and unsafe streets. This project begins to change that—delivering faster buses, safer corridors and a system that respects the urgency of people’s lives. Because when transit works, opportunity is no longer out of reach—it arrives on time.”</p>
<p>“I’m grateful to Mayor Mamdani, NYC DOT, and DDC for advancing these important improvements along the Bx6 corridor in Manhattan, strengthening a critical connection between Manhattan and the Bronx,” said <b>Manhattan Borough President Brad Hoylman-Sigal</b>. “With Opening Day here, it’s especially important that we’re investing in faster, more reliable bus service and safer streets for the thousands of New Yorkers traveling between our boroughs each day. I look forward to the benefits for riders and neighborhoods on both sides of the Harlem River.”</p>
<p>“Get ready for a strike down the middle! Better bus service and safer streets go hand in hand, and this project delivers both,” said <b>New York City Council Majority Leader Shaun Abreu</b>. “This is an important step from the City to deliver on its promise of fast, reliable buses. I&#39;m excited to see this investment in protected, center-running bus lanes and look forward to working with the Mayor to bring more projects like this to neighborhoods across the city.”</p>
<p>“Fully protected center-running bus lanes, plus other upgrades for speed, safety and comfort, are good news for Bronx riders and show the type of commitment riders want to see citywide,” said <b>Betsy Plum, Executive Director, Riders Alliance</b>. “We look forward to the rollout this spring and are eager to see these bus service improvements show up in our lives and take root in our community. Projects like these that save time and dignify bus commutes are an essential part of building a city that all New Yorkers can afford.”</p>
<p>“The Bx6 is a critical crosstown corridor whose buses have been moving too slowly for far too long,” said <b>Ben Furnas, Executive Director, Transportation Alternatives</b>. “We&#39;re thrilled this project will include a fully-protected two-way center-running bus lane — a gold-standard design which will speed up travel for tens of thousands of New Yorkers, including those trying to catch the game at Yankee Stadium! Paired with new safety infrastructure for pedestrians and cyclists, this ambitious project will bring much-needed upgrades to the streets of the Bronx.”  </p>
<p style="	text-align: center;
">### </p>

</div>

    

</div>
